<div id="review_500765391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/500765391" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14778159-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574406694p2/14778159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/500765391?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500765391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13537541235226057722"><b>
  <u>***Update July 22, 2013***</u>
</b><br/>Upon reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23522.Mythology' title='Mythology by Edith Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mythology</a> by Edith Hamilton for my summer reading assignment, this specific quote has come to my attention:<br/><br/><blockquote>
<i>"Triton was the trumpeter of the sea. His trumpet was a great shell. <b>He was the son of Poseidon and Amphitrite.</b>"</i> (38)</blockquote> <br/>Really, Anna Banks? Really? You couldn't even get the basic facts down? (For those who haven't read this, she claimed that Triton and Poseidon are brothers. Why? That's beyond me.) Now I <i>for sure</i> won't be reading the next book.<br/>____</span>
  <span id="freeText13537541235226057722" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>***Update July 22, 2013***</u>
</b><br>Upon reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23522.Mythology" title="Mythology by Edith Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Mythology</a> by Edith Hamilton for my summer reading assignment, this specific quote has come to my attention:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"Triton was the trumpeter of the sea. His trumpet was a great shell. <b>He was the son of Poseidon and Amphitrite.</b>"</i> (38)</blockquote> <br>Really, Anna Banks? Really? You couldn't even get the basic facts down? (For those who haven't read this, she claimed that Triton and Poseidon are brothers. Why? That's beyond me.) Now I <i>for sure</i> won't be reading the next book.<br>_____________________<br><br>Congratulations, Of Poseidon! You have been honored with a rating of 1 star from me, an honor I don't give lightly!<br><br>Admittedly, this is how I view <s>mermaids</s> Syrena:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404319i/786702.jpg" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even <i>after</i> I read this book, I <i>still</i> view them like that, since it’s not like we were given a good, detailed description of Syrena.<br><br>Like other shitty paranormals, strip this book of its (minimal) paranormal elements, and you get an angst-ridden teenage stereotypical romance that is painful to read about. Of Poseidon didn't even execute the paranormal aspects well, which is why it was so easy to notice that it was merely a sexist, angsty-romance book disguised as a fantasy about <s>mermaids</s> Syrena. <br><br>The characters in this book were flat and irritating. Sorry, Anna Banks, it takes <i>a lot</i> more than describing how utterly hot Galen is; he has to have a personality other than being a total jerk. He has to be <u>fleshed out</u>. Got that? The only things I know about him is that he loves answering questions with questions and loves Emma’s lips.<br><br>Even worse, we had to endure through his point of view. Most of the time he was just lusting over Emma’s lips, and let me tell you, it was complete torture.<br><br>Emma was okay at some times, but at others, she was plain stupid and actually listened to <s>idiot</s> Galen. At first, she was against Reyna being forced to marry Toraf, but then, she started <i>helping</i> him, claiming Reyna was playing hard-to-get. And you know, the author made it seem like it was <i>bad</i> that Reyna was not submitting to Toraf like she was supposed to be, and she wasn't doing what her job was as a women and having kids. *eye roll* I probably wasn't meant to, but I was actually rooting for Reyna, until she, sadly, eventually ended up with Toraf. Sexist, much?<br><br>This is the kind of thing that makes me want to pull my hair out. According to this book, it’s a bad thing that Reyna wanted to choose her husband by herself, not forced to marry a man she didn't want. Grr!<br><br>The secondary characters were useless and I have no idea why they were even there.<br><br>Like I brought up earlier, the author didn't do a very good job of introducing us to the Syrena, except that they are one sexist species. They spent barely any time underwater, and we know very minimal about the world they live in. <br><br>I wish there was some sort of conflict between the descendants of Triton and Poseidon. They kept referring to some kind of ancient vendetta between the two, but they never actually had any fights. That would have made the story much better. <br><br>Who’s the antagonist? I've no clue. There was no major conflict whatsoever. The revelation at the end was <i>very</i> anticlimactic and didn't make much sense. It kind of just came out of the blue without much foreshadowing. I wasn't surprised, I wasn't flabbergasted, I was <i>indifferent</i>. I didn't care at all.<br><br>In short, this was a pointless read. You know it’s a horrible book when you find yourself questioning why you bothered to read a book, which is what happened to me with <i>Of Poseidon</i>. There wasn't any conflict, the plot was basically non-existent, and the only reason one would want to read this is if they want to read about “hot” Syrena. Not if you actually want to read an intriguing story on the nature of Syrena, because that is obviously too much to ask. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13537541235226057722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15428323349951196968" style="display:none">This was a quick and easy read. <div id="review_287277368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287277368" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287277368?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those deserving of cruel and unusual punishment</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christina (A Reader of Fictions) by: </span>
      no one. I brought this pain on myself.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287277368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16652497354475546548">Originally posted <a href='http://readeroffictions.blogspot.com/2012/05/under-sea-from-little-mermaid.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>I really, really would like to find a mermaid book that I like a lot, but that search will be continuing. Of Poseidon is a book that most readers are probably going to love or be entirely annoyed by. Banks has a definite style, one that will either amuse and enchant you, or that will make you roll your eyes vigorously over and over again. For me, it was the latter.<br/><br/>Problem one is the host of YA tropes in the characters and their relationship to one another. Emma, a card-car</span>
  <span id="freeText16652497354475546548" style="display:none">Originally posted <a href="http://readeroffictions.blogspot.com/2012/05/under-sea-from-little-mermaid.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />I really, really would like to find a mermaid book that I like a lot, but that search will be continuing. Of Poseidon is a book that most readers are probably going to love or be entirely annoyed by. Banks has a definite style, one that will either amuse and enchant you, or that will make you roll your eyes vigorously over and over again. For me, it was the latter.<br /><br />Problem one is the host of YA tropes in the characters and their relationship to one another. Emma, a card-carrying member of the Bella Swan school of heroines, is exceedingly clumsy: "I'm betting Cinderella didn't feel this foolish, but then again, Cinderella wasn't as clumsy as an intoxicated walrus" (2). Note, too, Banks' sense of humor. This pretty much captures it perfectly. Emma meets Galen, Syrena prince, by tripping and smashing her face into his chest. We are treated to these inner thoughts:<br /><br /> "Tripping is bad enough. Tripping into someone is much worse. But if that someone has a body that could make sculpted statues jealous—and thinks you've broken your nose on one of his pecs—well, that's when tripping runs a distant second to humane euthanasia." (5)<br /><br />This girl seriously needs to sort out her priorities. Also, she spends way too long thinking about the awkwardness of the situation. While she's thinking, she remains plastered against him, because obviously that's less weird. Everyone trips sometimes. He would laugh and move on if it were the real world. It's not though, so no one's phased by how long she presses her face against his chest on first acquaintance. Here's one more quote to explain my distaste for Emma: "If stupid were a disease, I'd have died of it by now" (119). This attitude is so unhealthy. I encourage girls not to think of themselves this way, even as a joke.<br /><br />Galen, of course, is drawn to her from first meeting, purportedly because his mermaid (sorry, Syrena) senses are tingling. Meant to be together, blah, blah, blah. They met while she was on vacation (during which time her best friend got eaten by a shark). She goes back to Jersey and he shows up in her school with an identical schedule. When she tries to avoid him after the first class let out, he grabbed her wrist and, when she tries to pull away, he grips harder (41). This is a primo sign of a controlling guy. I was not surprised to learn that he had 'serial-killer eyes' (290). Among his other charming qualities, he also bosses her around constantly and takes advantage of her memory loss to convince her to accompany him somewhere.<br /><br />I would also like to point out that Emma completely forgets about Chloe's death and that she's supposed to be sad within a day of Galen's showing up at her school. Meanwhile, her mother hears that Emma tripped and hit her head, freaks out and accuses Emma of sleeping with Galen, her boyfriend. The two are not dating and she refuses to believe anything else. He was a transfer; it was his first damn day at that school. WHAT WHAT WHAT?<br /><br />The other big problem I have is the inconsistency of what the Syrena know about humans. Galen is an ambassador to the humans, which basically means a spy. He is bewildered by: phone books, people having more than one name (first and last), lip gloss, and countries. At the same time, he is capable of using a phone (likely a fancy modern one) and driving a car (note: one with a manual transmission). He was also capable of passing all of the high school classes she was taking. Plausibility fail.<br /><br />Of Poseidon had some seriously major flaws, as I've pointed out, but it was still a quick and enjoyable read. I suspect many people will enjoy it more than I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16652497354475546548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2291153896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Bonnie Shores" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Shores" href="/user/show/25177308-bonnie-shores">Bonnie Shores</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291153896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer301803663070331199">This review is for all three books—Of Poseidon, Of Triton and Of Neptune—because I read them in quick succession, because I didn't want to stop to write a review. 🤩<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482417625ra/21515380.gif' width='600' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the "tale" of Emma, a high school senior, who learns that she is half Syrena <i>(it's a mermaid/merman, but don't say that to their face)</i> after meeting Galen, a gorgeous Syrena prince, who is allowed to visit land in order to study humans. Emma literally bumped into Galen on a beach in Florida where she and her best friend were v</span>
  <span id="freeText301803663070331199" style="display:none">This review is for all three books—Of Poseidon, Of Triton and Of Neptune—because I read them in quick succession, because I didn't want to stop to write a review. 🤩<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482417625ra/21515380.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the "tale" of Emma, a high school senior, who learns that she is half Syrena <i>(it's a mermaid/merman, but don't say that to their face)</i> after meeting Galen, a gorgeous Syrena prince, who is allowed to visit land in order to study humans. Emma literally bumped into Galen on a beach in Florida where she and her best friend were vacationing before school started. Shortly after that, something horrible happens and Emma is distraught.<br><br>Fast forward to the first day of school back in New Jersey. Emma is sitting morosely in class when guess who walks in? If you said Galen, you'd be right! He realized upon meeting her over the summer, after seeing her lavender eyes and feeling "the pull", that she was Syrena, and he needed to investigate further.<br><br>Things don't go smoothly between them at first. Galen isn't human and he never seems to know the right thing to say or do. Plus, he's in all her classes (on purpose) and he comes off like a stalker. Things are different under the sea.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519068439ra/25089042.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Needless to say, after several misunderstandings, they start hanging out, and Galen reveals her secret. Since she's only half Syrena, she can't form a tail, so, at first, she doesn't believe him. <b>AND</b> she's more than a little freaked out when she sees his.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519066730ra/25088955.gif" width="600" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But as she spends more and more time in the water, realizing that she can breathe and talk, she accepts what she is. Much of the first book is spent trying to discover who Emma's real parents are, since she figures it couldn't possibly be the only mom and dad she ever knew. We're also introduced to Galen's twin sister, Rayna, and her mate, Toraf (LOVE him 😍), as well as Rachel, the human woman whom Galen saved from drowning when he was a "fingerling". She used to work for The Mob and has an abundance of talents which she uses to assist Galen. This includes selling underwater treasures that Galen brings her, which makes him a ton of money. She plays his mom and does all the necessary human things for him, including purchasing his house and car, enrolling him in school, etc.<br><br>The second book picks up where the cliffhanger ending from the first book leaves off. Emma finds out who her mother is (her father had died when she was 15) and misunderstandings abound. When Galen and his older brother, Grom, the king, and the rest of the crew finally catch up with Emma and her mom, the truth of everything is revealed. But just when you anticipate a happy ending, things back in the underwater kingdom go awry. The future looks dim for the royals, as treacherous plots come to light, and Emma's half-breed existence is forcibly revealed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444691414ra/16535891.gif" width="600" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The final book in the trilogy brings Emma and Galen to Neptune, a small town in Tennessee, where full-bloods and half-breeds coexist peacefully on land (next to lots of fresh water lakes and rivers), unbeknownst to their salt water brethren. The first person they meet is Reed, a friendly half-breed who has obvious eyes for Emma. After being invited (and going) to Reed's family's home for dinner, Galen is unhappy about being in Nepture. Later that evening, Galen and Emma have an argument, he leaves, and the adventure begins.<br><br>I really loved this series and highly recommend it to anyone who loves sweet and innocent YA romance. All the characters were well-written and the author gives you the chance to get to know each of them pretty well (relative to their importance in the story). This was my first mermaid book and I thought the author did a great job of making that world believable.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497152548ra/22993076.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="301803663070331199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_330935638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/330935638" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3485363-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378208886p2/3485363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/330935638?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/3485363-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer330935638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10845469187881423967">2.5 out of 5<br/><br/>As seen on: <a href='http://www.thebookosaur.com/2012/05/review-of-poseidon-by-anna-banks/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookosaur</a><br/><br/>I picked up <em>Of Poseidon</em> for one reason and one reason only: The Little Mermaid. I watched The Little Mermaid so much when I was little that every time I see a dinglehopper, err.. a fork, I'm tempted to <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tpDgWm4HBW8' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>comb my hair</a>. Suffice it to say, when <em>Of Poseidon</em> made it onto my radar, I fell for the premise - hook, line and sinker. <em>Of Poseidon</em> is your average fish out of water story - literally. Galen, a Syrena prince, is sent to land in search of a girl who supposedly poss</span>
  <span id="freeText10845469187881423967" style="display:none">2.5 out of 5<br /><br />As seen on: <a href="http://www.thebookosaur.com/2012/05/review-of-poseidon-by-anna-banks/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookosaur</a><br /><br />I picked up <em>Of Poseidon</em> for one reason and one reason only: The Little Mermaid. I watched The Little Mermaid so much when I was little that every time I see a dinglehopper, err.. a fork, I'm tempted to <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tpDgWm4HBW8" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">comb my hair</a>. Suffice it to say, when <em>Of Poseidon</em> made it onto my radar, I fell for the premise - hook, line and sinker. <em>Of Poseidon</em> is your average fish out of water story - literally. Galen, a Syrena prince, is sent to land in search of a girl who supposedly possesses the Gift of Poseidon, a gift that's extremely rare and allows her to communicate with fish. The sea is divided into two kingdoms: the House of Poseidon and the House of Triton, and the fish whisperer is the key to uniting these two kingdoms. Despite this kick-ass premise, however, <em>Of Poseidon </em>failed to deliver. It started out promising, but, like a fish out of water, it flopped around for a bit, making sad fishy faces, until, sooner rather than later, it came gill-to-gill with its maker.<br /><br />So, what didn't work? I've read a lot of young adult novels, covering a lot of different genres and supernatural beings. Vampires? Obviously. Werewolves? You betcha. Angels? <del>Regretfully</del> Admittedly, yes. Fairies? Witches? Magicians? Check, check, triple check. The only supernatural protagonist I hadn't come across before is merfolk, or Syrena, as they are called in <em>Of Poseidon</em>. After reading <em>Of Poseidon</em>, I think I now realize why this is: An underwater story is hard to do, for a number of reasons:<br /><br />1. Female Association: Call them what you like, but if they have a human upper body, a fin for a lower body, and live under the sea, they are merpeople, and referring to them as Syrena is not going to change that fact. Blame it on society, on Disney, or on whatever or whomever you like, but merpeople are typically associated with females. Despite the numerous references to Galen's defined muscles, the width of his shoulders, and the strength of his arms, all of his manly qualities instantly went out the window with the flick of his fin.<br /><br />2. World-Building: For the underwater scenes, I expected to be blown away. About 70% of the planet is covered in ocean, and "<a href="http://www.noaa.gov/ocean.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">more than 95 percent of the underwater world remains unexplored.</a>" I think I need to reiterate this fact: <em>Ninety-five percent of the underwater world is unexplored</em>. Do you know what that means? For an author, that's basically a free pass to create any world that they so desire. This is an author's chance to unleash their imagination. To go wild - and, more importantly, to get away with it. Who am I to argue with the world the author creates, when absolutely anything is possible? I was expecting my mind to be blown by the underwater world in <em>Of Poseidon -</em> I wanted fantastical landscapes and bizarre and unique creatures, but instead all I got was a boring cave and the Titanic.<br /><br />3. Merman/mermaid lore opens up a whole smorgasbord of questions that I really don't want answered, let alone even want to think about. Like what, exactly, do they eat? In <em>Of Poseidon</em>, this question is answered, but I'm not sure if I particularly like the answer. Also, <em>where</em> do they go to the washroom? And <em>how</em>, technically speaking, do they perform this necessity? What do you call a group of mermaids? A pod? A school? A mermish club? Lastly, the most disturbing question of all, since the Syrena in <em>Of Poseidon</em> are able to change back and forth between their fish form and a human body, where does the male's "eel" and the female's "clam" go when in fish form?<br /><br />But that's not all. The non-underwater-related stuff is lacking too, ranging from the language to relationships to faulty logic:<br /><br />1. Language:<br /><br />(1) If I never hear someone say "Ohmysweetgoodness" again, it will be too soon. In total, there's 324 pages in my ARC of <em>Of Poseidon</em>, and I counted 12 Ohmysweetgoodnesses throughout the book, which averages out to be exactly one Ohmysweetgoodness for every 27 pages. If this were a drinking game, and I had to take a shot every time Emma said "Ohmysweetgoodness", I'd have passed out before I got a third of the way through (eight of these instances happened in the first 100 pages). Throw in a few variations of "freaking" - yeah-freaking-right, unfreakingbelievable, fanfreakingtastic - and it's enough to drive someone mad. I can't tell you what these numbers mean statistically speaking, but it really puts a damper on a reader's enjoyment, linguistically speaking.<br /><br />(2) Projectile vomit is mentioned, not once, not twice, but three times. There are <em>three</em> references to explosive vomit! My brain can't even fathom this right now. I can maybe handle one instance, possibly two, but I draw the line at the third. Here's a little sample from my copy: "...vomit explodes everywhere. The drain can't handle the volume" (p. 208 of ARC). Vomiting, especially of the explosive variety, is something that should be done behind closed doors, in private. It's not something that I should read about in the pages of my young adult novel. I can deal with the I-can't-be-with-you love story, the platonic love interest, the unreasonable logic that seems to plague teenagers, but I cannot, will not, deal with nasty bodily fluids, especially when it has absolutely nothing to do with the story line.<br /><br />2. Relationships: Believe it or not, there is not one healthy relationship in the entire novel. Galen and Emma's relationship is based on one big lie, and Emma is constantly playing games with Galen and Galen is constantly telling Emma what she can and cannot do. As for the secondary characters, it's bad enough that Rayna is wed to Toraf without her consent, but she wasn't even present at their mating ceremony. But the weirdest relationship of them all is between Emma and her mother. Emma's mother plays Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde so well that even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51496.Dr_Jekyll_and_Mr_Hyde" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Louis Stevenson</a> would be impressed. One minute, she's the good cop, doting lovingly on her daughter, and within the next minute she's the bad cop, accusing Emma of sleeping with Galen and asking her if he beats her (ummm what? This lady is totally out to lunch).<br /><br />3. This novel also suffers from convenience, faulty logic, and absentee parents. Let's <em>pretend</em> we're dating, because otherwise no one would understand why we are spending so much time together. Oh, also, let's make sure we kiss in front of our parents, otherwise they will seriously doubt our dating status and we wouldn't be able to hang out anymore. I don't know about you, but when I was a teenager, kissing my boyfriend in front of my parents pretty well had the opposite effect. It didn't warm the cockles of my mom's heart to see her little girl making out with her hormone-infested, think-with-the-other-head boyfriend. No, such an act pretty well guarantees three things: for the mother, a mental image of 16 and pregnant; for the offending daughter, a stern talking to and a no closing your bedroom door policy; and for the father, inspiration to clean the gun collection. When you're a teenager, the last thing you want is for your parents to catch you making out, which is why the gods created high school dances and house parties. But none of this even matters, anyway, because Emma's mom is conveniently never home.<br /><br />I apologize for the long-winded rant, I didn't think that's where this review was headed when I started it, but I should have had an idea since I wrote six pages of notes while reading <em>Of Poseidon</em> and the majority of my bullet points end in these characters: !?!?!?!?!?!??!!?!?!? Despite my obvious qualms with this book, there were some aspects that I did enjoy; after all, I did rate it a 2.5. So, where did those two and a half stars come from, exactly?<br /><br />Things I liked:<br /><br />1. The humour: The humour in this novel is really what kept me reading until the end. The Syrena's descriptions of human activity is particularly notable.<br /><br />2. The premise: It's really very unique and unlike anything I've read.<br /><br />3. The insults: You can't go wrong with insults like slithering eel, minnow, and tadpole.<br /><br />4. The setting: Emma is from the Jersey Shore and for the life of me I couldn't help but picture a bunch of mermaids fist pumping the shit out of <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jgA2xo0HYrE" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Sea</a>.<br /><br />Bottom line is this: With the influx of underwater stories, I'd recommend tossing this one back - there's plenty of other fish in the sea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10845469187881423967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_788689309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/788689309" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/788689309?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer788689309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer92113778502043982">Read the full non-spoilery review @<a href='http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com/2014/06/of-poseidon-by-anna-banks-syrena-legacy.html#more' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Perfection Called Books</a><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374209ra/728169.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Concept:<br/><br/>I was a bit hesitant to read this book because whenever I think of mermaids, wait, I don't think of mermaids! That's just it. It seems like such a childish idea/fantasy, it's something I haven't though about since the days of watching The Little Mermaid. I didn't think I'd like this book because it focuses on mermaids, but I did end up liking it! The mer-people in this book are called Syrena. There's forbidden romance, myste</span>
  <span id="freeText92113778502043982" style="display:none">Read the full non-spoilery review @<a href="http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com/2014/06/of-poseidon-by-anna-banks-syrena-legacy.html#more" rel="nofollow noopener">A Perfection Called Books</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374209ra/728169.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Concept:<br><br>I was a bit hesitant to read this book because whenever I think of mermaids, wait, I don't think of mermaids! That's just it. It seems like such a childish idea/fantasy, it's something I haven't though about since the days of watching The Little Mermaid. I didn't think I'd like this book because it focuses on mermaids, but I did end up liking it! The mer-people in this book are called Syrena. There's forbidden romance, mystery, snark, and more! And that's all I'm saying. Go read ;) <br><br>The Writing:<br><br>I was a bit confused and put-off by the dual POV because Emma's side is told in first person while Galen's is told in third person. Either have them both in first person or both in third person. It made Galen seem so impersonal, and it was harder to connect with him than Emma. It was easier to deduce more of the story from Galen's POV though. The writing was simple and plain and good. There were some really hilarious and witty moments so I commend Banks for that. I wish that Banks explored more of the Syrena world, but I guess this book was more about Emma discovering her gift. Next book perhaps? <br><br>The Plot: <br><br>To me it seemed that the plot was dragging in parts. Sometimes I felt that this book focused too much on the romance and less on developing characters and an actual plot/storyline. The plot was a bit predictable but still enjoyable. Overall though a plot did eventually form. It was fascinating learning more about the Syrena race and their story. <br><br>The Characters:<br><br>Emma - This girl had a 180 personality change within the first 20 pages. She went from sweet and innocent to feisty and stubborn. I find that HIGHLY unrealistic. But besides that, I do like Emma. She gets a bit on my nerves sometimes, but overall I like the girl. She's not weak like some other protagonists. *cough* NORA GREY *cough* She's strong and although she gets all weak in the knees near Galen, she knows how to snap out of it and call him out when he's being too controlling. <br><br>Galen - Whoa this guy is hot. That was my first thought. I really like Galen. He's protective and thoughtful and smart. He's clear-headed and sweet. He's not afraid to say what he feels. I HATE how sometimes his overprotectiveness turns him into a domineering person. Chill out, dude. <br><br>The Romance:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389060210ra/7980601.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The romance in this book was really cute, but I felt that it happened way too quickly. Emma and Galen are an adorable couple, and I think they complement each other well. It's a bit hypocritical of me, but gosh it took forever for them to kiss!! All that sexual tension. I was like "Just kiss already!!"<br><br>The Ending: <br><br>Things got crazy near the end!! It all happened so fast. The ending isn't exactly a cliffhanger, but it's really good. <br><br>This book is light and fun, so if you're looking for a book to get you out of a reading slump, this is the book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="92113778502043982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_675870783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/675870783" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/675870783?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781742972817" href="/book/show/13573520-of-poseidon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675870783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1171315833407203082">This review also appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/10/24/of-poseidon-by-anna-banks-review-featuring-the-densest-mermaid-ever/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews!<br/><br/>This is what happens when I don’t heed the advice of my most trusted book buddies. A book like Of Poseidon comes along and many hours are wasted on its torturous and infuriating pages. The start was really promising, with Emma and her friend Chloe literally stumbling into a super attractive guy called Galen. Galen happens to be a royal Syrena (or merman) from the House of Triton, and he believes that Emma is a Syrena wit</span>
  <span id="freeText1171315833407203082" style="display:none">This review also appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/10/24/of-poseidon-by-anna-banks-review-featuring-the-densest-mermaid-ever/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews!<br><br>This is what happens when I don’t heed the advice of my most trusted book buddies. A book like Of Poseidon comes along and many hours are wasted on its torturous and infuriating pages. The start was really promising, with Emma and her friend Chloe literally stumbling into a super attractive guy called Galen. Galen happens to be a royal Syrena (or merman) from the House of Triton, and he believes that Emma is a Syrena with her characteristic violet eyes and gift of Poseidon, where she can talk to sea creatures.<br><br>In preparation of this review, I have earmarked 16 pages throughout the book.<br><br><b>What I enjoyed about Of Poseidon</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382608898ra/6058727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- <b>The mermaid mythology.</b> Mermaids seem to be the next big thing, and this one was my first. I quite enjoyed the details about Syrena, how they sift and find their next mate to ensure the continuity of their species. Having the Triton and the Poseidon as rival houses with different powers was interesting too (although I’m not quite sure how they are rivals but also perfect mates)<br><br>- <b>The cute ocean references.</b> The syrena have really cute terms of endearment scattered throughout the book, like angelfish, swearing by Triton’s trident, minnow, and the dreaded stonefish.<br><br>- <b>Evocative oceanic scenes</b>. Of Poseidon features some great underwater scenes of interacting with the aquatic creatures that are there and even diving deep below to the bowels of the ocean. I loved the part where they explored the Titanic and discovered Emma’s power with prolonged time under the ocean.<br><br><b>What I didn’t enjoy about Of Poseidon</b><br><br><b>Warning: spoilers and ranting ahead.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381674832ra/5176207.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- <b>Interchanging third and first person perspectives.</b> This made the book really hard to get into, with Emma’s perspective in first person and Galen’s perspective in third person. The flow of the book was somewhat interrupted and sometimes when you are reading about one person, the plot jumps when it goes into the next person’s perspective.<br><br>- <b>Emma’s constant temper tantrums.</b> For a girl who is supposedly known to be sweet in class, she has a huge temper and throws unreasonable tantrums throughout the book. She throws Rayna, Galen’s sister through a glass door with murderous intentions, and after fighting she’s whimpering within seconds. Emma is quick to judge and go off at other people, especially Galen, and can’t even stick to her beliefs either. One second, she blows up about Rayna being forced into marriage, and the next second she’s helping the husband Toraf with making her jealous. Whhhattt?!<br><br>- <b>Emma’s absolute denseness.</b> Throughout the book, her sheer stupidity was evident. When Galen suggests that she might be adopted due to her Syrena traits, she believes him over her own mother, even when she produces photographic evidence of her birth with both parents present, and her birth certificate. WHY? Not to mention this:<br><br><i>You’d think they’d notice my heart is on the opposite side of my chest. I mean are you sure you’re reading this right? You’re not a human doctor, you’re basically a veterinarian right? You could be wrong.</i><br><br>Because according to Emma, vets don’t know which side a humans’ heart is.<br><br>- <b>Galen’s possessiveness.</b> Besides being obsessed with her red lips and Syrena heritage, the only reason Galen is sticking around is to find out whether she really is Of Poseidon and I’m just saving her for my brother. When Emma breaks up with him, he stalks her, blows up her phone, beats up the guy she’s with and makes serial-killer eyes. Not to mention his sexist philosophy:<br><br><i>He scours his memory for a sweet-natured Syrena who would take care of him, who would do whatever he asked, who would never argue with him.</i> <br><br>- <b>Eye-rolling goodness.</b> Emma constantly uses the phrase Ohmysweetgoodness and constantly blushes at every thought of Galen. As soon as the two break up, Galen literally gets hoarded by “a hurricane of teenage females” girls texting him, propositioning him, “touching him, giggling at him, smiling at him for no reason, and distracting him…”<br><br>- <b>Way ahead of the plot reveal.</b> How come Emma can’t summon her fin but she can breath underwater? Why does she have the traits of a human but have the Gift of Poseidon? I don’t know, maybe because she’s a half-breed? After Xrays, testing of Emma’s gift, checking of the heart rate and the pulse, they finally come to this conclusion, and it’s dragged over two chapters, like it wasn’t already half obvious.<br><br>- <b>Completing brushing over the best friend’s death.</b> Instead of mourning her friend who got eaten by a shark, Emma quickly transitions into daydreaming about dating Galen and thinking of ways to get him to kiss her. Not to mention the mother encouraging her thoughts towards Galen. Since when is a hot guy more important than a close friend’s death??<br><br>Suffice to say, I can’t really recommend Of Poseidon. I’ve suffered through way too many Bella Swans and annoying main characters and Emma was possibly one of the worst. There were many scenes that seemed to be really immature with Galen, Emma and even Emma’s mum doing or saying things that were rash, juvenile and self-centered. That being said, I know some people really loved the mermaid mythology and oceanic scenes. Unfortunately, I have the next book on my shelf waiting to be reviewed, so I’ll have to read it sometime.<br><br>Thank you to Hardie Grant Egmont for sending me this book in exchange for an honest review!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1171315833407203082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_843097238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/843097238" />
    <a title="Carlie K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28260702-carlie-k"><img alt="Carlie K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481472798p2/28260702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/843097238?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carlie K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carlie K" href="/user/show/28260702-carlie-k">Carlie K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer843097238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13986071906523335686">3.75 stars<br/>-----------------------------------------------<br/>This review is originally posted on <a href='http://www.candythebookishgirl.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bookish Girl</a><br/>-----------------------------------------------<br/>You can get this book on <a href='http://www.bookdepository.com/Poseidon-Anna-Banks/9781250003324/?a_aid=thebookishgirl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookdepository</a><br/>-----------------------------------------------<br/>I first picked up this series because I thought it had something to do with Greek Mythology, which I’m obsessed with. As it turned out, there was nothing “Greeky” about it. However, I can ensure you that this book is not a disappointment, but rather a surpri</span>
  <span id="freeText13986071906523335686" style="display:none">3.75 stars<br />-----------------------------------------------<br />This review is originally posted on <a href="http://www.candythebookishgirl.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bookish Girl</a><br />-----------------------------------------------<br />You can get this book on <a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/Poseidon-Anna-Banks/9781250003324/?a_aid=thebookishgirl" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookdepository</a><br />-----------------------------------------------<br />I first picked up this series because I thought it had something to do with Greek Mythology, which I’m obsessed with. As it turned out, there was nothing “Greeky” about it. However, I can ensure you that this book is not a disappointment, but rather a surprise.<br /><br />Our heroine, Emma, grows up thinking she is just another ordinary girl, except with a pair of violet eyes. One day, she meets Galen, a boy who shares the same purple eyes as hers. After a blood-filled accident and with the help of Galen, Emma finally starts seeing the truth, about herself and her family.<br /><br />The book starts off really well. It is funny and gripping. I was so into the book just like I was water being absorbed into a sponge. Miss Banks clearly knows how to work her magic to keep readers’ attention. Then when it comes to the middle, it lacks a good climax. There isn’t a single event that makes you feel excited or hold your breath because you’re nervous about how it goes. However, I did really enjoy the ending because it was kinda unexpected, since the book had been misleading me the whole time (ha ha).<br /><br />Now onto the characters. I liked Emma okay. She is like Tris, who keeps doing things people tell her not to do. But besides that, she is normally likable. Then it comes to Galen, whom I loved very much. He is gorgeous, funny and protective. Miss Banks did a great job to build up this character. I love to read about his psychology, how he is torn between his loyalty and duty towards his kingdom, and his feelings towards Emma. This makes Galen a very real character.<br /><br />Of Poseidon is an entertaining and fast-paced story filled with humor and surprises. It is a book that serves best as an enjoyable pick-me-up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13986071906523335686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_843097238'><a id="like_count_review_843097238" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/843097238?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">16 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12425532-of-poseidon">Like</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1061772039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1061772039" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17389678-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145890p2/17389678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1061772039?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/17389678-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061772039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2654195323862546840"><blockquote>
  <b> If you’re up for a good plot <i>idea</i> but odd and unflattering <i>execution</i> that manages to insult the female race with it’s promotion of patriarchalism, then this is your book.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>If, like me, all you’ve ever asked for is a mildly engaging plot, simple (I’m not asking for anyone to spew the dictionary) but fluid and concise writing with a sprinkling of tastefully used metaphors, a good grasp on tense and POV, characterisation that is either relatable or satirical and a little bit of common sense then</span>
  <span id="freeText2654195323862546840" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> If you’re up for a good plot <i>idea</i> but odd and unflattering <i>execution</i> that manages to insult the female race with it’s promotion of patriarchalism, then this is your book.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />If, like me, all you’ve ever asked for is a mildly engaging plot, simple (I’m not asking for anyone to spew the dictionary) but fluid and concise writing with a sprinkling of tastefully used metaphors, a good grasp on tense and POV, characterisation that is either relatable or satirical and a little bit of common sense then <b>turn away and don’t look back</b>. <br /><br />Honestly, the little checklist above is <i>very much achievable</i>. Hundreds, thousands, of stories fall within that scope. So I don’t get it. Am I, and others like me, being <i>too demanding?</i> Are we asking for Pulitzer quality literature? I don’t think so. I just think we’re out there for an enjoyable read. Personally, enjoyable ceases to be an emotion for me when a book looses track of certain elements from that checklist. <i>Of Poseidon</i> allows <b>all</b> of said elements to slither away. It doesn’t even attempt to beg for them to come back. <br /><br /><i>Of Poseidon</i> tackles the mermaids, something quite rare in YA. Well isn’t that just the first clue. It’s rare because it’s, to be honest, a little hard to wrap the mind around. <b>Half fishes</b> are what you’re telling everyone to fall in love with (I’m making a generalised statement, in that every YA seems to sneak in that love interest that the protagonist, and the reader, is technically meant to<i> “fall head over heels”</i> for—I’m not buying it). I can’t wrap my head around that. But I love me some mythology. Poseidon, Triton, opposing, feuding families, an ancient mystery—what more could you want? Well everything and anything, that’s what. <br /><br />Lovely average (but really, a <b>Mary Sue</b>) Emma hits Miami for a vacay with her best friend for life, Chloe. There she runs into hunky spunky Gallen (or the merman in question) who happens to be running a diplomatic errand for the people of Syrena (oh gee, he’s looking for Emma but he just doesn’t know it yet). As fate might have it, they find one another, get their bloody lives tangled up and lo and behold, there’s a generation of mystery, lost loves, arranged marriages. The works, really. <br /><br /><blockquote>Let’s start off with the most dominant problem: <b>Point of View and Tense</b>. </blockquote><br /><br />For those missing out on the fun that is I, I’m a <b>fan of third person POV</b>. I see no wrong with it. Third person is a nurturing POV for the imagination. You can take your book places with third; you’re not limited. <b>The world is your oyster</b>. But then I see those that <b>butcher my baby</b> and I just cry out<b> “How?!”</b> (Dare you…—that bit is implied) Because honestly, <b>how?</b> You literally have the world at your feet. It’s an impersonal, detached narrator who is, without bias, recounting the scenes. <b>With third person, you can have greater room for SHOWING rather than TELLING</b>. It’s the bloody golden rule of writing. It’s beautiful, third (I’m going to stop my ode to this POV soon). Point is, I was shocked because <b><i>Of Poseidon</i> violently destroys my favourite POV bit by bit, mercilessly and without care to my heart.</b> Unbelievable. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> This is written in two <i>ALTERNATING</i> POVs. Emma’s POV is 1st person. Gallen’s is in 3rd person. And wait for it: This book is written in <i>PRESENT TENSE</i>. </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Someone hold my heart because I did not think there could ever again be a combination of POV and tense that I will hate more in the world. Why would you even do such a thing?! Here’s the thing: 1st person in present tense is normal. No qualms. But <b>3rd person in present tense does this thing where it DOESN’T WORK</b>. Do you know what present tense does to 3rd person? Wait, let me rehash that. <b>DO YOU KNOW WHAT PRESENT TENSE DOES TO 3RD PERSON WRITTEN WITH TOO MANY SENTENCES BEGINNING WITH “He this…”, “She that…”?</b> No? Well let me give you a clue: <b>It dips my favourite tense into a pot of blood and takes it out into the middle of the bloody ocean, drops it in the sea and says “Good luck with life, but you’re most probably, in fact definitely, am going to become a scrumptious meal for the killer sharks who peruse this part of the sea”. </b> You don’t do that to a point of view, you just don’t (especially not to my favourite one either. It gets personal then.) <br /><br />I think I’ve exhausted all that I can say on this issue. Alternating POVs—you know how I feel. I don’t like them. They complicate things, take away from the complexity of the story because then you’re struggling to remember what happens in each POV, if they detail separate situations, or often the narrators meld together into one voice (hardly happens in this one because 3rd person, but hey, that obviously has other issues going on), or it just juts the story all together. It all applies here. Alternating POVs don’t work in favour of <i>Of Poseidon</i>. But then again, don’t feel insulted. It hardly ever works anyway. <br /><br />We also get a return episode of my favourite show in the world:<b> “How to write teenage slang that, in reality, is an insult to our the teenager's intelligence”. </b> Thank you. Just when I thought I couldn’t get enough of that show. <br /><br />Here’s the thing, people, authors, have just got to stop overestimating the amount of “slang” that the average teenager uses. We are not a generation of senseless bubbleheads. We’ve got intelligence, ambition, a vocabulary that isn’t exclusive to the <i>urban dictionary</i>. And I most certainly do not say: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> Ohmysweetgoodness</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That’s a favourite of Emma’s. A personal concoction too, I would believe. My teacher of a mother would be insulted if she ever heard such a phrase come out of my mouth.<br /><br />But my biggest, overshadowing criticism would have to be the <b>revolting, completely obsessive and shocking secondary romance</b>. <br /><br />I don’t want to speak on anybody else’s behalf, but when I was <b>extremely</b> young, I liked to peruse the fanfiction archives. Back in the day, fanfiction had this trope that everyone and their mother’s overused: <b>the arranged marriage</b>. And boy did it sell like hotcakes. I’m saddened to say that the ignorant young me did read a fair few in her fanfiction course of life (but only a few because I had the <b>pickiest</b> criteria in the world which pretty much eliminated most stories unless they were worthy of a literary prize haha). <b>But I’ve grown so much since then and I’m now extremely hyperaware of how demeaning this trope is.</b><br /><br />No matter how you paint it, <b>Toraf and Rayna are not in a normal, healthy, supportive relationship</b>. <br /><br />If Toraf did to me any of what he did to Rayna, I’d leg it straight across the Indian Ocean (and running on water isn’t even possible so please, that’s saying something) just so I could get away from that creep. He goes <b>behind her back</b>, crawling to her brother, who just happens to be the <b>RULING PATRIARCH</b> (URGH THAT’S ANGER FOR ANOTHER DAY) and arranges his own mating (the equivalent of marriage), behind her back, <b>without her consent</b>, just because he <b>FEELS A BLOODY CONNECTION</b> and insists that she does too, <b>EVEN WHEN SHE HAS BLATANTLY STATED THAT SHE DOES NOT</b>. Her brother happily agrees because <b>HE DECIDES</b> that she’s past the normal mating age (<b>BY TWO YEARS</b> ONLY. I’M SO INSULTED) and so naturally she must be rejected goods and they might as well pair her up before her <i>ovaries shrivel up and drop out. </i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “I’ve been waiting for the day I could make Rayna someone else’s problem,” Grom says. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Shut the front door. My mouth is hanging open in utter disgust. How dare he?! Here’s a fact of life, Grom: <b>Women are not hot pieces of property that you’ve got to sell it while the price is high because once it regresses, you’re doomed.</b> WOMEN DO NOT BELONG TO MEN. Unbelievable, this book. Unbelievable. <br /><br />And just when we think certain character’s like Emma protest such an idea, we then have it counteracted because apparently, obsessive or not, Toraf and Rayna are kind of “cute”/made for each other (let’s not quote me on this. I know Emma says a line like this. In fact, I’m 100% positive. I just can’t be bothered to find the exact quote). And so, pardon the french but, fucked up or not, this relationship can suddenly be condoned. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> What a disgusting move that just regresses all progress with equality back to the damn middle ages.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />And here’s where I just become plain nit-picky:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Ah, we have a history buff. Very nice, Ms. McIntosh.” </i>
    <b></b>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Um how about no. All she did was know the year the Titantic sunk. POP CULTURE has ensured that we all know when the Titantic sunk. If that’s the criteria for a history buff then I’ll be damned, I’m a bloody history professor then. <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br />Emma lives in a beachside town so, as the stereotype goes, she’s all about the <b>flip flop</b>. Those who have read my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20759498.Compulsion" title="Compulsion by Martina Boone" rel="nofollow noopener">Compulsion</a> would know that <b>I HATE FLIP FLOP STORIES</b>. I’ve got this little aversion to feet. And all accessories concerning them. It’s a personal thing. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “The only thing you know about me is that I’m life threatening in flip-flops.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Well don’t wear them, Einstein. Emma loves her flip-flops. They cause her much danger. To that I say, “I told you so.” <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “…Us girls are tricky creatures”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book singlehandedly destroys all we’ve worked for to gain equality. How peachy brilliant. I’m sorry, I wasn’t aware that FEMALES, WOMEN, WERE <b>CREATURES</b>. I’m fuming. Really. <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br />Midway through, there is a chapter (Number 11 ) that is written, for more than half the duration, in <b>RHETORICAL QUESTIONS</b>. Why would you do that? (Har. Hardy har, har. Do you see what I did. I amuse myself) Rhetorical questions are the type of things that you’ve got to use carefully, tastefully and mindfully. I get that they’re the perfect means of posing all these questions that you want the audience to ask themselves, but mother of all things on earth, I don’t need a boatload of it dumped on my head. <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br />Emma is as Mary Sue as you can get. She’s practically the poster child. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “You said I’m special. How special am I?” <br />He takes in a breath and lets it out slowly. “Very.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Oh wow. You’ve told me so much. Basically, if you’ve got no time for Mary then let this one go. <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br />And lastly, because I’ve got no patience to get any angrier than I already am (and because it’s hitting 1 am) let me end it with this insult: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “…He never acts like this.” Except that time he beat Toraf like a stepchild on the beach when he kissed me. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />If my mouth could hang any lower, it would probably dislocate. I said I wanted a good simile. I DIDN’T ASK FOR AN INSULTING STEREOTYPE THAT HAS ME EVEN MORE DISGUSTED THAN I ALREADY AM. How dare anyone insinuate that stepchildren are beaten? HOW DARE ANYONE?! <br /><br />Ψ<br /><br />There is pretty much one pro to this story and it would be the great snark. Emma’s a snarky character. I like that. It adds a bit of humour in between my sandwich of insulted and revulsion. Thanks for the variation, I guess. <br /><br />ΨΨ<br /><br />Point is, if you’re extremely socially conscious then <b>SKIP THIS BOOK</b> because you will die of shock and even I couldn’t resurrect you (because I’ll most probably be gone as well). I’ve been left insulted, both my intelligence and my beliefs, and cannot believe that this book went there. <br /><br />The plot was going to go somewhere but boy, did this book miss the mark. Don’t read it for the patriarchal themes. They’re vulgar. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2654195323862546840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_217805509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217805509" />
    <a title="Debbie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5098369-debbie"><img alt="Debbie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589209937p2/5098369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217805509?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie " href="/user/show/5098369-debbie">Debbie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217805509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16149450500462683573">If you think the cover of Of Poseidon is beautiful, just wait till you start reading this amazingly beautiful novel. Anna Banks has written a captivating story. The romance between Galen and Emma will capture your heart. I could not put this novel down. Anna Banks’ writing is beautiful. This is the best word to describe this novel perfectly…"Beautiful". Of Poseidon is told from Emma’s and Galen's point of view, and this made the story so much deeper for me. I love to see both characters’ thought</span>
  <span id="freeText16149450500462683573" style="display:none">If you think the cover of Of Poseidon is beautiful, just wait till you start reading this amazingly beautiful novel. Anna Banks has written a captivating story. The romance between Galen and Emma will capture your heart. I could not put this novel down. Anna Banks’ writing is beautiful. This is the best word to describe this novel perfectly…"Beautiful". Of Poseidon is told from Emma’s and Galen's point of view, and this made the story so much deeper for me. I love to see both characters’ thoughts in a novel. And to see what Galen was going through with his feeling for Emma, and the same for Emma, to see her feelings for Galen, just made my heart break for these two. I wasn't ready for this book to end, and with the cliffhanger ripping my heart out for Galen, I will be waiting for the next book to mend it. *Sigh*<br /><br />Emma’s summer vacation to Florida with her best friend Chloe turns into the nightmare she never wanted to live, especially after her father’s death two years before. When she meets Galen, the most gorgeous guy she’s ever seen, on this vacation, then he shows up at her school, she soon realizes the nightmare is only just beginning. Galen has to find out if Emma is the gift of Poseidon that will reunite the house of Poseidon and the house of Triton. But Prince Galen isn't ready for this twenty first century thinking girl, and Emma’s not about to take orders from this prince of the sea.<br /><br />Galen is an awesome guy, even if he is behind the times with Emma and her world above the sea. But one thing stays the same no matter which world or time you live in, and that's love. Galen is going to have to sacrifice what he loves the most to save his people and his brother, but Galen’s sacrifice might be more than he can live with. Galen’s and Emma’s romance took my breath away. Galen is the kind of guy that all us girls wish we could be romanced by. His love for Emma is one of protection: no one will take what is his. I love Galen's old-fashion chivalry and the way he loves Emma. Anna Banks had my heart swooning for Galen, and wishing for my own Prince Galen.<br /><br />There’s also another romance going on with Rayna, who is Galen's sister, and Toraf. This couple is the hilarious side romance to Galen’s and Emma's heart-melting one. I love Anna Banks for giving me two romances to swoon over: one for tears and one for laughs. Rayna and Toraf will have you laughing, but I did feel so sorry for Toraf at times. Although there's no way you can not help but to fall in love with Toraf, Toraf takes a lickin’ and keeps on going, determined to win Rayna's heart<br /><br />Of Poseidon is a beautiful romance of Galen’s sacrifice for his love for Emma with a fantastic adventure with merfolk of the sea. I have to give a teaser to show a little of who Galen’s and Emma's characters are: <br /><br />"He can't even find his class in a school with only three halls. That he found me clear across the country seems more miraculous than a push-up bra." <br /><br />I highly recommend Of Poseidon as a must read. . <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16149450500462683573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17141846017921428152">Wow, it's been a very long time since I finished a book in that record-of-a-time.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book, awesome debut to the series and the way it ended; kinda of a i-knew-it moment, but I couldn't put my hands on it before,, I like how Anna Banks left to be unraveled until the very last pages.<br/>The Mythology in the story is awesome, I'm obsessed with all things Poseidon so ... *cheers*<br/>I loved how easy it was to get into this book, how simple the story started off and very interesting to keep</span>
  <span id="freeText17141846017921428152" style="display:none">Wow, it's been a very long time since I finished a book in that record-of-a-time.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book, awesome debut to the series and the way it ended; kinda of a i-knew-it moment, but I couldn't put my hands on it before,, I like how Anna Banks left to be unraveled until the very last pages.<br />The Mythology in the story is awesome, I'm obsessed with all things Poseidon so ... *cheers*<br />I loved how easy it was to get into this book, how simple the story started off and very interesting to keep reading yet not so brainy. <br />The characters were a bit two dimensional for me, which adds up to light-reading-thing, enjoyable-at-the-same-time thing I was just talking about. <br />I expect we'll see more and more with the next installment and I'm getting to it as soon as possible.</span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1233203784">
  <td colspan="2">
    <div class="updateActionLinks">

<div id="review_2845334932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2845334932" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2845334932?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250027368" href="/book/show/16059484-of-poseidon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2845334932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16460784585901720909">This was such a fun and unexpected read! I thought the idea sounded interesting but I was worried what the execution would be like. I had absolutely nothing to worry about though because it was great. I loved the whole idea and concept, it drew me in right from the start and was incredibly interesting. My only minor complaint is that I didn’t really LOVE the characters, I only liked them and it took away from my enjoyment a teeny bit. Other than that, it was great! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_304590275" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304590275" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304590275?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304590275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7813511212448573399">Of Poseidon is just Not For Me. I see all those four and five star ratings and wonder WTF is wrong with me? This book did not make me happy. Beyond ‘Syrena’ and what not were people who each had something stupid to say and or do.<br/><br/>The one thing <b>I could have liked</b> was how both the girls pointed out just how wrong the boys acted. I mean who wants to be stalked? Who wants a controlling, manipulative person hanging over them? Both Galen and Toraf act like douches… and the girls knew it. The problem is</span>
  <span id="freeText7813511212448573399" style="display:none">Of Poseidon is just Not For Me. I see all those four and five star ratings and wonder WTF is wrong with me? This book did not make me happy. Beyond ‘Syrena’ and what not were people who each had something stupid to say and or do.<br><br>The one thing <b>I could have liked</b> was how both the girls pointed out just how wrong the boys acted. I mean who wants to be stalked? Who wants a controlling, manipulative person hanging over them? Both Galen and Toraf act like douches… and the girls knew it. The problem is despite acknowledging the same fact they still ended up, and I quote, <b>“One part hissy fit and one part swoon.”</b> <br><br><a href="http://www.gifbin.com/984240" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373882ra/727663.gif" alt="funny gifs" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And <b>I could have liked</b> Emma too given her being saucy and smart and funny at times... but… but… but the advise she gave about acting hard to get did not sit right with me. In fact, none of them sat right with; none of their actions at least. Her mother, Rachel and Rayna…. all said some pretty idiotic things to say. Does a girl only spend time with a boy to do the deed? Is the whole purpose of her being to date? Dear lord, why bother with the ruse of dating at all? Mother of god! Or Rayna… What? What? I liked the no-nonsense, my life= my choice stance that she came in with. But her eventual about face because she was jealous was just not right. AT. ALL. And Galen, dear misguided Galen. I didn't like him. He could simply be so condescending all the time! <br> <br>Actually, the idiocy was spread far and wide in this one. I finished it but only barely.<br><br>1/5<br>Thanks Net Galley! <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7813511212448573399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
